<pics>None< /pics><Date>1433917055627<//Date><user_id>106720951616376521421< /user_id>< user_name>
Roy Conrad< /user_name>
< review>
The lunch buffet is a steal at under $10 out the door, and the selection is pretty good. They keep the naan coming fresh out of the oven as you go. There are several options for both meat and non-meat eaters. The flavors are good but not amazing - but definitely good enough for the price tag.

Everytime I've been here the place has been relatively empty, so in and out is quick and easy, and it's easy to get the waitstaff's attention. If you're looking for a bustling social restaurant experience, this place is not for you (that it's been a while since I've been there, and that could have changed.

If you come after 3pm you have to order off of the dinner menu (no buffets), and the prices are in the $10-$20 range if I remember correctly. I've only come once for dinner because at dinner prices the place is less of a bargain.

I could drive a few minutes and go to my favorite place Tara's Himalayan and pay about the same, for exceptional flavor.

If I'm craving Indian and am in the area for lunch, it's a go.<//review>

< name>
Charlotte Maddox</name>
<Response>None<//Response><rating>3<//rating>< review>
The ambience could be a little better. Maybe it's a cultural thing, but I'm not a huge fan of red lighting at night. Makes me feel like I'm in a Redlight district or something. It was very dim, and the decorations were a bit outdated.

The service was good, and the family members who run it do a good job about making customers feel welcome. I got the chicken korma, which was $10. It came with rice, which is nice. However, the rice didn't taste like basmati rice, more like jasmine. The Korma itself was good, but didn't have a rich a flavoring as some of the other places I've been. Not sure if this is a more authentic version of the dish or not. My friend got a salad and the chicken tandoori, which he said he liked very much. I tried a bit, and found the chicken to be well-cooked and not bone-dry and hard.

The sweet lassi was delicious....my first time turning down mango lassi for something else.<//review>

< review>
We purchased our Rad Rovers about a year ago and I've been doing all the maintenance on them myself. However, the bikes were starting to feel sluggish and some of the repairs/tweaks were beyond my skillset. We reached out to Work Horse Bicycles and scheduled an appointment with them to service/repair our bikes. They did an absolutely phenomenal job. The bikes have never run so smooth and as fun as they are to ride, they are even better now than before. The customer service is excellent. I also want to mention that we scheduled our maintenance / repair about a week in advance. Several days before our appointment one of their techs called us to let us know they could get us in two days early if we wanted rather than waiting. That was really thoughtful and not very common with bike shops or repair shops in general. Great people. Great location. We will definitely be back!</review>

<review>Discovery of a slow leak in the 1" plastic water line between my meter and my house last weekend first prompted a call to a family member in the trades for a recommendation. After he said Val Betti was the only company he would recommend, I made a call to them Monday morning.

My wife had a very unpleasant experience here 2 days ago and yesterday.  Tues was National Sandwich Day.  (Yes, really.  :-)  It's a "thing"!)  She had a coupon from Subway on her phone valid until yesterday, buy a 12" sub and get one free.  They wouldn't honor it.  They said it had to be ordered online, which is not true. Not only was she treated condescendingly by the owner or manager, they lied, in that you do not have to order online to redeem the coupon.  There are other Subways around, so we won't be going to this one any longer.  Hopefully the corporate company understands that they have people like this running their shops.<//review>

<pictures>None</pictures>< review>
This park brings me fond memories of when I was a kid, The main feature of the park is an old aircraft that was used in Korea. It is quite different from what it was in about 1955 when I played on it, now it is completely sanitized. Back then it was all medal and glass as it came from the Air Force when retired.
The entire park is beautifully maintained and a pleasure to visit.</review>

114110375311111270883<//userid>
<username>Alan Burkes< /username>< time>
1512611535632<//time>
<Rating>4< /Rating>< review>
It's about as good as Sysco can get. Meaning you shouldn't expect anything that requires actual still to cook. The sandwich and pizza portions of the cafe are only open at lunch time, so unless you are here at that short time period,  pretend those sections don't exist.

That leaves you with two choices. There is a basic grill that offers hamburgers, chicken sandwiches, hot dogs, grilled portabella (vegan burger?). In the past they had cheese steak, but they have been out for the past few weeks.

There is also a rice restaurant. I call it a rice restaurant because it tries to be Japanese, Korean, and Thai all at once, which naturally means that it is neither. They sell sushi and rice bowls with mixed sauces and vegetable offerings. I guess if you called their sushi Kimbap and their rice bowl Bibimbap, you could call them Korean.

The secret is that the rice place is their best option, but they are much less popular than the grill because people love unhealthy food. It's a shame because they have some very good pickled vegetable options that make for a crunchy and satisfying meal.</review>
